<Text>We ordered our food, 3 burgers 1 fry, at 1:55pm. The cashier immediately flipped the screen around and asked for a tip. For what? For taking our order? Do they not get paid? I mean, I understand tipping at a restaurant where you are seated, drinks are brought out to you, you know? Service? But what am I tipping for? Do gas pumps ask for a tip? Does the walmart cashier ask for a tip? Does In-N-Out ask for a tip? I am all for tipping, but immediately after you place your order?
The place was not busy at all, there were no orders ahead of us. One guy was working the grill while the cashier dude was on his cell phone. 20 minutes later at 2:15 I walked up and asked if everything was okay, the cashier guy said that a big "Uber Eats" order came in and those have priority and that our food would be out shortly.
I don't mind spending $4.75 on a burger, but by no means was what we received $4.75 burgers. They were not even warm, asked for "no catsup" came with catsup anyway. And I was not expecting the "Little Big Burger" to be quite as "Little" as it was.
I cant imagine a place like this staying in business for long. I'm sure enough people's curiosity has kept a steady flow of customers up until this point, but with prices, product, and service at the level of what I experienced, I doubt they get many return visitors.

The first time visiting Little Big Burger I was attracted by how you can see the person cooking your food like how In and Out does. The staff is super friendly and helped me figure out what kind of burger I wanted by saying how they cook their burgers to what condiments you want on it. <review>In short, there are many items that need to be resolved for this place to stay in business. The quality of their product will make me a repeat customer, but the frequency of my visits will depend on their ability to overcome their many flaws.

My family visited twice on opening day--once at noon and again at 6:30PM. In both cases, there were less than six people in line and we waited over 20 minutes each time to just place our order. After ordering the first time, our drink order was fulfilled in under 5 minutes. During our evening visit, we waited 15 minutes for our ice cream after ordering. The wait time the second time around was due to the lack of employees, and one person playing "one man band" behind the counter (answering questions from both customers and the untrained cashier, giving samples, scooping ice cream, calling out orders, and running cups back and forth from the register to the kitchen).

The things that need to change ASAP and shouldn't cost the company significant dollars:
- Two employees (cashier and "runner") are not enough to take care of customers. Have more staff behind the counter to answer questions, provide ice cream samples, and start taking drink/ice cream orders before customers reach the cashier. During slower hours, these employees can also clean the bathrooms, empty trash, and interact with customers (rather than just apologize for taking so long). Doing the little things goes a long way for the customer experience.
- Train your cashiers on how to use the POS system properly. This creates a large bottleneck.
- Have your drink stickers print directly to the kitchen area. Currently, the labels print at the cashier, they have to put the labels on cups, and then have them run them to the kitchen window (about 15-20 feet away).

Changes that would be nice:
- If things remain busy, run two cash registers.
- Widen the section for those standing in line. There is currently very narrow standing room and it would be a nightmare for someone with claustrophobia or young kids.
- Open earlier. People may not want ice cream at 10:00am, but they will definitely would drink boba tea at that time.
- Stay open later (til 9:00 or 10:00pm?). Your most likely demographic is 15-30 year olds---think about it. Most boba shops in the area stay open until 9-11pm on weeknights
- Add a Vietnamese Iced Coffee DRINK to the menu. The VIC ice cream is awesome... but I'd come back 3x a week if there was a drink to go with it.
- Don't charge customers extra for adding a regular boba. "Boba" is in your name, yet you add an up-charge when people want it in their drink. Specialty add-ins deserve to be marked up.
- Add a customer loyalty program to reward repeat visitors.
- Don't raise your drink prices. Currently Sweet Lab is on the high end of pricing for their teas. Most of your competitors are charging $2.75-3.50 for regular sized milk tea (boba included) with an extra $0.50-0.75 if they are ordering a larger size.
- Run regular specials. This can encourage new customers to come in and get returning customers to try new drinks/ice creams.

I plan to go again in the next several days and hopefully will be able to change my review for the better. With the right changes, this local business should be able to thrive!<//review>< user_name>
Ryan Thomas<//user_name>

<username>Christopher Allsup</username><Time>1576805321776<//Time>< rate>
5< /rate>
< review>
My first experience with Nor-Cal Hobbies, won me over.  I walked in, knowing no one. I had an older Kyosho I was looking to repair so I could use it as a loaner car. I would be buying a new model in the very near future.

The fact that I was able to walk in, speak with a staff person who knew the position I was up against, and allowed me to have some time just looking over parts to cobble together a fix. Was absolutely amazing. Needless to say, I've come back over and over again. I started as putting together a couple of older vehicles just to have something to bash. To being on a path of a regular on the track, and being at racing event.

What a great way to be reignited back into the hobby. And have access to an indoor track that is constantly changing.

You'll find the staff extremely knowledgeable from small drones, up to 1/5 scale nitro powered, and Crawlers. Seriously consider a visit.

Thanks Nor-Cal Staff,
You folks are amazing!< /review>

<user_name>Tony Bugna< /user_name><user_id>113056954148162296802</user_id><pics>None</pics>< Review>
Nor-Cal Hobbies and Race Place is handsdown one of the best hobby shops I've ever been to or seen. There are a ton of hobby shops in the US, in California alone but none that you will see that offer the Hands-On and honest opinions of the guys over at NorCal. They're not there to try and sell you the most expensive thing or try to get you to buy something that you aren't even interested in but rather get you set up with what you're looking for or something similar or better quality. From recreational to racing the guy is over there have it down pat. If it's your first time buying an RC car they will set you up with a very affordable and fun kit or if you've been Racing for many years and just looking for an honest opinion I know that personally Eric Vasutin and Anthony Bruno will give you their honest opinion on what they believe is the best available product for your needs. Even if it's something that they don't personally run themselves but they know would be better suited for you they won't hesitate to suggest it. And if they don't happen to have it in stock they will go out of their way to make sure they get you what you're looking for and if they don't have the ability to they will guide you in the right direction to obtaining what you're looking for. I'm lucky to say that this is my local hobby shop and there's not a lot of people as fortunate as I am to have a hobby shop like this available at their fingertips. With all that being said they also provide racing of all sorts whether it be off road carpet racing, on road racing, all the way to no prep drag racing they offer a wide range ways to make sure that you get the most fun out of your toy and hobby. If you're ever around San Jose take a minute to stop by even if it is just for a minute because I guarantee you that day that you are looking for something RC related you'll definitely be happy that you know of NorCal<//Review>

<Rate>5<//Rate><review>My first experience with Nor-Cal Hobbies, won me over.  I walked in, knowing no one. I had an older Kyosho I was looking to repair so I could use it as a loaner car. I would be buying a new model in the very near future.

The fact that I was able to walk in, speak with a staff person who knew the position I was up against, and allowed me to have some time just looking over parts to cobble together a fix. Was absolutely amazing. Needless to say, I've come back over and over again. I started as putting together a couple of older vehicles just to have something to bash. To being on a path of a regular on the track, and being at racing event.

What a great way to be reignited back into the hobby. And have access to an indoor track that is constantly changing.

You'll find the staff extremely knowledgeable from small drones, up to 1/5 scale nitro powered, and Crawlers. Seriously consider a visit.

Thanks Nor-Cal Staff,

Really good, patient service, very fair prices.

Both Adam and Dakota have taken the time to give us great education & advice, really focusing on what we were looking for.  I learned a lot and ended up with a car that really matched what I wanted.

Had an issue with a new car and they bent over backwards to keep us running while we waited for a manufacturer replacement to arrive... And the shop took care of the exchange, it was effortless for us.

Essentially the only R/C shop anywhere San Jose, seeing as the hobby has become a dying breed. The staff are very well-informed and ready to help with anything from off the shelf cars to the craziest custom builds. While their in-house track has its limitations, it does serve as a nice hub for competitive racing as well as casual use.</Review>

Very knowledgeable and helpful staff.  Store is usually well-stocked with common replacement items as well as upgrades, car kits, ready-to-run packages, and anything a RC enthusiast might need.  If what you need isn't in stock, it can be ordered very easily.

When we started RC cars as a hobby, NorCal Hobbies was our first stop. The selection, and helpfulness of the staff was awesome so there was no need to go anywhere else. <Rate>1<//Rate>< text>
If I could give negative infinity starts, I would.  We hired Olympia after our mortgage company spent a year of refusing our payments due to the flooding  and the loss of our home to flooding (twice).  Our mortgage company says the home as a complete loss despite our county buying us out and moved to foreclose on the property- despite refusing our payments.  We agreed to let Hal Jeffery's and Sam Branco's team help us.

They stopped the auction, but never finished up the agreement which was to negotiate a new payment with our mortgage company.  We have not heard anything since March 13th, in the evening. Due to our house being a buyout property and we were relocated by the US government, the SBA could choose to foreclose and liquidate our current home as well, despite never missing payments on either mortgage.   They gave us documents to file, which we paid $300 for, but only received four pages.  We later learned that they were suppose to have given us an entire packet to file, which is why they ask for all of your financial information.

Needless to say, in addition to $3,000 in their fees, we are out $600 in fees to stop the auction of a house that is to be torn down by the county at some point.  The worst part of it all is our lender keeps sending us letters say we are willing to work with you, while last we heard from Sam Branco on March 13, they were going to call our lender again and call us right back.  All of our emails and phone calls have gone unanswered since then.

What their "plan of action" to stop the foreclosure was has caused so many credit problems, that it will be years before we will ever recover from.   This left us both wondering if it was worth doing the right thing with a flooded home and holding out for the buyout.   It really is offensive that they are fully aware of our situation and then they too take advantage of a family that has lost everything twice.

I am sharing this in hopes that others will consider the ramifications of one, hiring this law firm, despite the google reviews; and two, to consider the financial ramifications for what they suggest to stop an auction or foreclosure.

Lastly, don't just read my review or the reviews on google, look on Yelp and any other board that provides consumer feed back.  Olympia cannot can't spam bot them all into good ratings.</text>

<Text>Hello there!

On day three of our trip to California, we decided to head to Huntington Beach for the day. We really enjoy Huntington Beach and it was only a 30 minute drive from our hotel in Anaheim.  The beach is great and the local shops are fun to browse and the even the neighborhoods are nice to take a stroll through.

Of course, we wanted to eat, something my husband and I do well, and often, especially on trips.

As we walked Main Street to make our decision of where we would eat, we decided on Sugar Shack Cafe at 213 Main Street, Huntington Beach, CA.

Since it was breakfast, not that it matters, my husband opted for the Spanish Omelet and I had the Kepper's Benedict.

We both agreed that the Keeper's was better than the Spanish Omelet. The sauce that was on the omelet was not that great. It tasted and looked like a watery tomato juice. Even the flavor of the omelet was not that great.

We sat outside and enjoyed watching people pass by as we ate.

The service was there, the hostess and waitress were nice and the atmosphere was great. Being from Tucson, we are not fans of sitting outside to eat - the heat is a little much but in Huntington Bach sitting outside was enjoyable with the breeze and the temperature.

All in all it was good. Just a little disappointing in the omelet. Little flavor and some watery sauce.< /Text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP7M_uUCh2-bIK1v021EQlNEhuF53xJXtzacrBR=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOFECrl6dCnHWVTLDIC6tyFYpyh6v7huhSK5Qme=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN2oG_r_VF96c53nHCwjeJSxLcYsFQv9V33eIiG=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPkk0MuVJkB6bwj_vhUhx23ZNGycEHNC__jKgtW=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP2e-Sj6A7eR6NlLYSkOEWVkuNp2co1mYG36Ttv=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPJfbhE3rXoi8u_-v7DAWPwn5-MB1Vsx1h4fsFn=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOL6lAnZUzs2xtL_dt6TK4QPGuLgUZYd1ML8tcF=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPNqA2csxd1116HAy7ZhMIzuaxtEi-1uO-G7ES0=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM5F1dAtie7rXfD6OgCX7BYbjDnO6jLtKIG5ahI=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOVARS4lNbO1CxLBadpNh3dQdCZ9uvqQ7W_G-kM=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics><Resp>None< /Resp><gmap_id>0x80dd214162ec8ced:0x7ffe8c595904074f</gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Sugar Shack Cafe is a great place to have breakfast in Huntington Beach.  The servers are friendly, the food always comes out quick and hot, and they don't skimp on the food they serve you.

There are three dining areas on the premises.  The first and most notable is their front patio.  This is a great place to people watch.  You may have to sign in and wait, to sit in this area, as it's the most popular.  Inside is always cramped, but they have some great old surfing photos of Huntington Beach on the walls to gander at.  There is a fairly large patio in the back, where you usually won't have to wait to be seated.

My favorite here is a ham, mushroom & Swiss cheese omelette.  This beauty comes out oozing with cheese, packed with smoky ham steak chunks and sliced sauteed mushrooms.  Very buttery tasting, as well.  YUM.  Hash browns are perfectly golden brown & crispy.

My wife and I would come here early on the weekend, whenever we were headed to Bolsa Chica Ecological Reserve, to do some birding.  If you can get here around 8am on weekends, then you'll beat the rush.  Parking can be difficult to find on Main St., but they do have several parking garages close by on Main St., just north of the Sugar Shack, one on each side of the street.

They are also famous for their French toast here.  So yummy!<//review>

<Review>Hello there!

On day three of our trip to California, we decided to head to Huntington Beach for the day. We really enjoy Huntington Beach and it was only a 30 minute drive from our hotel in Anaheim.  The beach is great and the local shops are fun to browse and the even the neighborhoods are nice to take a stroll through.

Of course, we wanted to eat, something my husband and I do well, and often, especially on trips.

As we walked Main Street to make our decision of where we would eat, we decided on Sugar Shack Cafe at 213 Main Street, Huntington Beach, CA.

Since it was breakfast, not that it matters, my husband opted for the Spanish Omelet and I had the Kepper's Benedict.

We both agreed that the Keeper's was better than the Spanish Omelet. The sauce that was on the omelet was not that great. It tasted and looked like a watery tomato juice. Even the flavor of the omelet was not that great.

We sat outside and enjoyed watching people pass by as we ate.

The service was there, the hostess and waitress were nice and the atmosphere was great. Being from Tucson, we are not fans of sitting outside to eat - the heat is a little much but in Huntington Bach sitting outside was enjoyable with the breeze and the temperature.

All in all it was good. Just a little disappointing in the omelet. Little flavor and some watery sauce.< /Review>< name>
Randal and Jesus Higby-Giron<//name>

< text>
URGENT/ BE AWARE!
My husband and I were in the Sugar Shack yesterday 9.13.19 for an enjoyable breakfast, when our order came it was very concerning. There was obvious mold on the two slices of bread, the eggs were under cooked and it continues from there. As my husband was eating he realized the food seemed very off and he first sent the toast back, the waiter noticed the mold and was nice about accepting it back. Another server brought back more toast however, it was evident it came from the same loaf just at the tail end.
My dish did not taste fresh and I left all of it behind. My husband had eaten one of the two eggs and left his meal aside. We payed our bill and left very disappointed as we have been residents in HB for 3 decades.
Shortly after, my husband became violently ill, unable to function. He was taken to the ER after a half day of torture and the doctor confirmed it was a food borne illness. I called the restaurant today hoping to notify the owner and I was told he is never around.
I am urgently writing this message because I do not want any person or child to go through what my husband just experienced. Food poisoning can be extremely dangerous.
If you are the owner reading this please FIX IT,  you are putting our community in danger. Thank you! MM< /text>

<name>Deanna Fountain< /name><Time>1514492919613</Time><rating>4< /rating>< review>
Sugar Shack is the true staple of breakfast places in downtown Huntington Beach. You get tasty food for a decent value, huge portions, and you're by the sea.

Their food is pretty much diner food. Nothing fancy but it satisfies hungry people happily. Their hash-browns cannot be beat. Their "surf" (half hot chocolate half coffee drink) is my guilty pleasure.

Whether you want a simple two egg breakfast with toast or something for a bigger appetite they have it all. I've had every kind of breakfast imaginable there and have not been disappointed.

They have outdoor seating both front (on Main St.) and back (in alleyway), as well as indoor seating. The indoor seating is first come first serve even on busy days.< /review>

< Text>
This is a great place. It's been around since 1967. They only serve breakfast and lunch but somehow have managed to stay in business when so many others have gone out or business. It's a local spot that has the support of the community. The food is really good and I've tasted most things on the menu over the years. It's always packed so get here early. It's worth the wait. They have a back seating area that usually is less packed than the front that has a view of main Street.< /Text>

< text>
Popped in for an impromptu brunch date on a Monday morning. The weather was finally sunny and we had opted to sit on the patio. Note: They do offer 2 patio areas. While the main (front) patio area is the most popular choice, they also have a back area covered patio as well.

I found our table to be pretty dirty for a restaurant. There was definitely a lot of food on the floor under our table which was a little gross to me. Looking past that, we placed our food orders...

We ordered the main street burrito and the keppler's. Both items came out pretty fast after we ordered. The food was okay, but nothing great and nothing that left me thinking wow - I have to have more of this.

The service was friendly, but we felt like we lost our waiter a few times.

Overall, the food was okay, but nothing that was amazing for me to come back again and gloat about.< /text>

<Date>1451504143123</Date><Rating>4</Rating><text>My extended family has been going here for years and I can see why!

Sugar Shack offers a good selection of breakfast items with very generous portions.

Plus, there's something on the menu for everyone, from the straightforward "eggs and bacon" types to those looking for healthier and lighter breakfast options.

The food was prepared well and the wait for both seating and food was minimal, despite mornings being fairly busy here due to the joint's increasing popularity.  The service was adequate and coffee was refilled when needed.

During busier times, this place is best suited for couples and smaller groups of 6 or less.

All in all, it's not the fanciest place to eat on the strip, nor is it the next taste sensation, but Sugar Shack is definitely good at what they do and that's delivering above-average breakfasts at a fairly reasonable price (considering the area)!</text><Pics>None< /Pics>< Resp>

<rating>2</rating>< review>
Fun little place to sit outside on the sidewalk and people watch. The back patio has it's charm but the overwhelming odor of refuse can be jolting as it occasionally wafts in the direction of patrons. The food is average tasting and there are plenty of choices. Don't try to communicate a food allergy, however. The message of needing to have NO dairy,  communited more than one time, didn't get  through and my vacation was cut short by three days as I recovered from the unfortunate effects. I won't be returning but give this place a try at least once and decide for yourself.<//review>

< review>
Love going to the Sugar Shack! Went this past weekend and disappointed to experience they have gone cheap on something like Ketchup! May not be a big deal to some else but when you like it on scrambled eggs, omlettes, hash browns or fries it makes a difference. It was like soup and ruined the meal experience. I don't mind refillable bottles like they have on the table for the ketchup. Just don't refill them and try to pass it off as no one will notice or care. If they cut corners there where else are they cutting corners? Charge me a few cents more but don't go cheap! I work in the restaurant industry and know the difference between condiment qualities. This was the cheapest you can buy. Sorry to have to write this post!</review>

< Review>
Love going to the Sugar Shack! Went this past weekend and disappointed to experience they have gone cheap on something like Ketchup! May not be a big deal to some else but when you like it on scrambled eggs, omlettes, hash browns or fries it makes a difference. It was like soup and ruined the meal experience. I don't mind refillable bottles like they have on the table for the ketchup. Just don't refill them and try to pass it off as no one will notice or care. If they cut corners there where else are they cutting corners? Charge me a few cents more but don't go cheap! I work in the restaurant industry and know the difference between condiment qualities. This was the cheapest you can buy. Sorry to have to write this post!< /Review>

One of the things I was most upset about when we moved from Massachusetts was losing the breakfast joint that we often frequented (ya know, right after moving away from my family! Lol). If there is any meal that my little family likes to go out for, it's definitely breakfast and it has to be bomb!

Well, you can imagine how quickly I entered the realm of morning glory when we found Sugar Shack. The food here is amazing. I love the HSS special. It's a super delicious grilled ham, scrambled egg, and cheddar cheese breakfast sandwich that I like to add a little avocado too. Sooooo good. I still haven't had a chance to try their breakfast burrito, but I totally want to.

The people that work there are laid back and efficient. There's a nice outdoor patio on Main St and another covered patio in the back. Quick service. Great food. What else could you ask for? Oh... would you also like one of the nicest beaches in America?? Well it's really close to the beach, so if you are looking for delicious morning time food before heading there, this is the place!

< text>
-Wait time was to be expected it's a popular spot.
-Staff was excellent, seating is tight, not a great place for groups larger than 4 or 5 (7 of us all together, jammed into a 4 person table on the patio). It was really sunny so definitely bring some sunscreen if you're sitting outside.
-Park further up Main Street or on a side street and walk in, parking always bad the closer to PCH you get.
-Food came out pretty fast for a busy restaurant.
Got the eggs Benedict. Everyghing tasted very fresh, ham was exceptional. English muffin wasn't overcooked. What just made it alright was the hollandaise sauce. It was just  bland to my taste buds. I really love a tangy hollandaise sauce. Everyone else seemed to really love their food so next time I go I'll try the a breakfast burrito or omelette I think.
3-stars for just okay food. If you're a big water the eggs Benedict will leave you hungry, only comes with hash browns.</text>
